def test_search_file_multiple_matches(tmp_path):
    """Test search_file with multiple matches in the same file."""
    temp_file_path = tmp_path / 'a.txt'
    temp_file_path.write_text('search term\nno match\nsearch term\nanother line\nsearch term here')

    with io.StringIO() as buf:
        with contextlib.redirect_stdout(buf):
            search_file('search term', str(temp_file_path))
        result = buf.getvalue()
    assert result is not None

    expected = f'[Found 3 matches for "search term" in {temp_file_path}]\n'
    expected += 'Line 1: search term\n'
    expected += 'Line 3: search term\n'
    expected += 'Line 5: search term here\n'
    expected += f'[End of matches for "search term" in {temp_file_path}]\n'
    assert result.split('\n') == expected.split('\n')

def test_search_file_with_current_file(tmp_path):
    """Test search_file using CURRENT_FILE when file_path is not provided."""
    temp_file_path = tmp_path / 'a.txt'
    temp_file_path.write_text('hello world\nno match here\nhello there')

    # Open the file first to set CURRENT_FILE
    with io.StringIO() as buf:
        with contextlib.redirect_stdout(buf):
            open_file(str(temp_file_path))

    # Now search without providing file_path (should use CURRENT_FILE)
    with io.StringIO() as buf:
        with contextlib.redirect_stdout(buf):
            search_file('hello')
        result = buf.getvalue()
    assert result is not None

    expected = f'[Found 2 matches for "hello" in {temp_file_path}]\n'
    expected += 'Line 1: hello world\n'
    expected += 'Line 3: hello there\n'
    expected += f'[End of matches for "hello" in {temp_file_path}]\n'
    assert result.split('\n') == expected.split('\n')
